## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables (x, v) and time t, matching second-order ODE models for nonlinear harmonic oscillators (restoring force depends nonlinearly on displacement and/or velocity, possibly with damping and external forcing). Typical relationships express dv_dt as a sum of restoring-force terms in x, damping terms in v, and optional time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke-type restoring acceleration, small oscillations)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Quadratic damping (drag-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (speed-squared resistive force)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (stick-slip / dry friction approximation)
- Duffing oscillator (softening/hardening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity + damping)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (strongly nonlinear conservative spring)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (nonlinear geometric restoring term)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle via nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping, self-oscillation)
- Driven damped oscillator (harmonic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (forced response and resonance)
- Duffing with drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (bistability/jumps under forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces often appear as odd functions of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*sin(c*x)), reflecting symmetry about x=0.
- Dissipation typically enters as terms opposing motion, commonly proportional to v (linear viscous) or v*Abs(v) (quadratic drag) or sign(v) (dry friction).
- Hardening vs softening behavior is suggested by the sign of the cubic stiffness term in -c*x - c*x**3 (frequency increasing vs decreasing with amplitude).
- Self-excited/limit-cycle oscillations are indicated by nonlinear damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v.
- External periodic driving is naturally represented by additive sin/cos terms in t, producing resonance, phase locking, and nonlinear response curves.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when the coefficient multiplying x varies periodically in time, i.e., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x.
- Strong geometric nonlinearities (e.g., pendulum) are captured by trigonometric restoring terms rather than polynomial stiffness expansions.
- Piecewise-like friction or impacts can be approximated by sign(v), Abs(v), or sharp nonlinearities, leading to non-smooth acceleration vs velocity.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO28)

GT: -c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5 - omega0**c6*x
Candidate formulas: 62

GT (fully expanded) is a fixed polynomial/monomial combination in \(x\), \(v\), and \(x|v|^{1/3}\), with **no \(t\)-dependence** and **no constant offset**:
\[
f(x,v)= -1.89974654282317\,v\;-\;3.43809390825923\,x^3\;-\;3.43809390825923\,x\,(0.0191974038845046|v|^{1/3}+1)\;-\;3.43809390825923\,x.

Expand the mixed term:
\[
-3.4380939\,x(0.0191974|v|^{1/3}+1)=-(3.4380939\cdot 0.0191974)\,x|v|^{1/3}-3.4380939\,x.
\]
So overall:
- coefficient of \(v\): \(-1.89974654282317\)
- coefficient of \(x^3\): \(-3.43809390825923\)
- coefficient of \(x|v|^{1/3}\): \(-3.43809390825923\cdot 0.0191974038845046\)
- coefficient of \(x\): \(-3.43809390825923-3.43809390825923=-6.87618781651846\)
- no other terms.

Compute the \(x|v|^{1/3}\) coefficient:

```python
3.43809390825923*0.0191974038845046
```

It equals \(0.065978\ldots\), so the GT coefficient is \(-0.065978\ldots\).

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–3
Each is the GT-like base plus an extra nonlinear term (exp/cos/log with \(t\), etc.). Since GT has **no such term**, we can set the multiplier of that extra term to 0 (their \(c4=0\)). Then they reduce to
\[
c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 v + c3 x|v|^{1/3},
\]
which can match GT by choosing coefficients appropriately (but note GT also has an \(x\) term; that’s covered by \(c0x\)). So **potentially match** after zeroing the extra term.

### Candidate 4
Has an extra \(\;c2\sin(c3 t+c4)\;\) term. To match GT for all \(t\), must set \(c2=0\). Then it becomes \(c0x+c1x^3+c5v+c6x|v|^{1/3}\), which can match GT. **Match possible**.

### Candidates 5–12, 14, 16, 18–23, 29–34, 37–38, 45, 47–49, 51, 53, 57–62
All include additional \(t\)-dependent terms, logs, rationals, trig, exponentials, etc. In every case, the extra term is multiplied by some free coefficient (e.g., \(c4\), \(c3\), etc.), so we can set that coefficient to **0** to remove the extra structure. After removal, most reduce to the same base linear combination of \(x\), \(x^3\), \(v\), and \(x|v|^{1/3}\) (or something that can be made so by also zeroing other extra coefficients). Therefore, for these, **a match is possible** provided the remaining skeleton includes exactly those four monomials and no others.

But we must be careful: some candidates have *different* skeletons (e.g., missing \(x|v|^{1/3}\), or having \(v\) duplicated but that’s fine, or having \(v^p\) that must be killed).

### Candidate 13
Extra term \(c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(c6 x+c7 v+c8)\). Set \(c4=0\) → base form, match possible.

### Candidate 15
Extra sine of log(abs(v)) term; set its prefactor \(c4=0\) → base form, match possible.

### Candidate 17, 21
Contain an extra sine term in \(x\) or \(v\); set its amplitude \(c2=0\) → base form, match possible.

### Candidate 24
Has an added constant \(+c4\). GT has no constant term, so set \(c4=0\). Then it is base form, match possible.

### Candidate 25–26
Contain \(+c3\exp(c4 v)\) or \(+c3\exp(c4 x)\). Set \(c3=0\) → base form, match possible.

### Candidate 27–28, 54–55
Have redundant linear terms (e.g., both \(c2 v\) and \(+c4 v\), or both \(c0x\) and \(+c4x\), plus possibly a constant). Redundancy is not a problem: choose them so the sum matches GT and set constants to 0. Match possible.

### Candidate 35
Form: \(c0x+c1x^3+c2v + c3\sin(c4x+c5)|v|^{1/3}\). The mixed term is \(\sin(\cdot)|v|^{1/3}\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\). There is no way to make \(\sin(c4x+c5)\) equal to \(x\) for all real \(x\). Setting \(c3=0\) removes the mixed term entirely, but GT needs a nonzero \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term. So **cannot match**.

### Candidate 36
Has \(c3 v^{c4}\) extra. Set \(c3=0\) and it becomes base form, match possible.

### Candidate 39
Has an extra \(c2 x^{c3}\). Set \(c2=0\) → base form, match possible.

### Candidate 40–42, 44, 46, 50, 52
These include extra monomials like \(v^{c4}x\), \(vx^2\), \(x|v|\), \(x^5\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), etc. In each case, those extra terms have free coefficients, so set them to 0, leaving (or allowing) the base form. Thus match possible.

### Candidate 41
Form: \(c0x^3 + c1 v + c2 x e^{c3|v|} + c4 v|v| + c5 x^{c6}|v|^{c7}\).
To match GT, we need an \(x\) term and an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term. We could try to use \(c5 x^{c6}|v|^{c7}\) with \(c6=1\), \(c7=1/3\) to get \(x|v|^{1/3}\). But we still need a pure \(x\) term; none exists unless we set \(c7=0\) to make \(x^{c6}\), but then we lose the mixed term. The \(x e^{c3|v|}\) cannot become \(x\) for all \(v\) unless \(c3=0\), in which case it becomes \(c2 x\) (good), but then we still need \(x|v|^{1/3}\) from the \(c5\) term (possible). Also must kill \(v|v|\) by \(c4=0\). So actually candidate 41 **can** match by:
- \(c3=0\) so \(c2 x e^{0}=c2 x\),
- \(c6=1,\;c7=1/3\) so \(c5 x|v|^{1/3}\),
- keep \(c0x^3\) and \(c1v\),
- set \(c4=0\).
Thus match possible.

### Candidate 43
Has \(x^3\sin(c3 v+c4)\), \(x\cos(c6 t)\), and log term times \(|v|^{c9}\). To match GT for all \(t\), must set \(c5=0\) (remove \(x\cos(c6 t)\)). To avoid non-polynomial dependence in \(v\) inside sine, must set \(c2=0\) (otherwise \(x^3\sin(\cdot)\) can’t equal a constant multiple of \(x^3\) for all \(v\)). Then we lose the \(x^3\) term unless there is another \(x^3\) term—there isn’t. So candidate 43 **cannot** match.

### Candidate 56
Exactly \(c0x+c1x^3+c2v+c3x|v|^{1/3}\). This matches GT by choosing:
- \(c2=-1.89974654282317\)
- \(c1=-3.43809390825923\)
- \(c0=-6.87618781651846\)
- \(c3=-(3.43809390825923\cdot 0.0191974038845046)\approx -0.065978\ldots\)
So **definite match**.
